# Memorandum of Agreement
# UFCW Local 7 & Safeway and Albertsons
## Mountain West Division
## RETAIL & MEAT
### July 5, 2025

UFCW Local 7 (the "Union") and Safeway/Albertsons (the "Employer") are parties to Collective Bargaining Agreements (the "CBAs") for retail and/or meat bargaining units in the state of Colorado and Rock Springs, Wyoming locations. The parties have met and reached a tentative agreement for new CBAs. Such new CBAs shall contain the provisions of the current CBAs between the parties, except as modified in the attached documents entitled "Tentative Agreement(s)" as well as any and all documents attached to, or incorporated by reference into, said Tentative Agreement(s). The new CBAs shall have a term of the date of ratification through and including January 8, 2028 (conforming dates for contracts with current expiration dates other than January 4, 2025). See the attached contract date table.

The attached Tentative Agreements and the current CBAs, as modified herein, represent the entire Agreement between the parties. The changed contract language set forth in these proposals represent changes to the Safeway Denver Retail Bargaining Unit language, these additions may appear in other Articles and/or Sections in outlying areas and other bargaining units. Any Union proposal not identified or addressed herein shall be deemed withdrawn. Any proposal of the Employer not identified or addressed herein shall be deemed withdrawn. The offer, modification, or withdrawal of any proposal in these negotiations shall not be used as evidence in any arbitration or other proceeding between or involving the parties.

The parties agree to carry forward all existing Letters of Understanding and Letters of Agreement, specifically including any Letters of Agreement reached during the term of the 2022-2025 agreement, except as otherwise set forth herein.

The parties reserve the right to correct any drafting errors or omissions in this Agreement.

The Union, its officers, and bargaining committee agree to recommend and support the ratification of this Agreement. The Union agrees to use its best efforts to vote the Denver bargaining units on or before July 11, 2025 and all remaining bargaining units not later than August 1, 2025. The Company's Division President agrees to issue a public statement before July 11 regarding its commitment to test the Committee recommended staffing program.

This Memorandum of Agreement is only effective upon ratification by the Union of this Agreement.

An associate's basket hours will not be reset by a lateral increase given in the progression. For example, an All Purpose Clerk employed in Aurora who has 3000 basket hours currently making $18.50 at ratification will receive a wage increase to $18.75 and then need to work an additional 640 hours until receiving a raise to $19.25.

The parties agree that the newly organized pharmacy technicians at Store 839 will be covered by all terms and conditions applicable to the Albertsons Denver Metro Clerks Bargaining Unit, as well as any terms and conditions of the Safeway Denver Metro Clerks Bargaining Unit specifically applicable to pharmacy technicians. The Safeway Denver pharmacy technician wage tables shall apply to Store 839. Pharmacy technicians at Store 839 as of the date of ratification shall be entitled to the wage rate that is the highest of: (1) the employee's wage rate at ratification, if it appears on the wage table, (2) the next higher wage rate on the wage table if the employee's wage rate at ratification does not appear on the wage table, (3) the wage rate the employee would otherwise be entitled, crediting the employee's basket hours and experience, or (4) if the employee is being paid higher than the Thereafter rate on the wage table, the employee shall be treated consistent with other above-scale employees as provided for in this Agreement. The Employer shall deliver to the Health Plan Administrator a "Promise to Pay" for newly added employees to ensure that no employee suffers a gap in coverage, and that health coverage under the Rocky Mountain Unions and Employers Health Benefit Trust shall commence retroactive to the ratification date for the newly accreted employees.

The Company agrees to pay a one-time award of $200.00 (gross) to all bargaining unit workers who have one (1) year or more of seniority as of August 1, 2025. Such payment shall be made as soon as possible following ratification.

### Return to Work

Effective upon ratification by all bargaining units, the Union and the Company, on behalf of themselves and their parents, subsidiaries, affiliates, officers, agents, members, and assigns, mutually release each other, as well as the other's parents, subsidiaries, affiliates, officers, agents, members, and assigns from any charges, grievances, claims, and causes of action of any type whatsoever which arise out of the negotiations of the 2025-2028 Collective Bargaining Agreements between the parties or the 2025 Unfair Labor Practice Strike conducted by the Union against the Company, including, but not limited to, any matters which were raised and/or could have been raised in grievances (except for Member Discipline and Pay), charges before the National Labor Relations Board or other applicable agency, and cases in any applicable court of law. Any and all such claims are released/and or dismissed as described herein on a non-precedent setting basis. The Union and Company also agree to withdraw any and all requests for information issued in connection with negotiations.

The Union makes an unconditional offer to return to work on behalf of all strikers, and will cease the strike, picketing and other action taken in connection with the strike. The Union agrees to pull down picket lines as soon as possible on Saturday, July 5, 2025. The Company will reinstate all strikers based upon the unconditional offer to return to work to the same positions, classifications, seniority and hire date they held prior to the date they ceased working. Workers will return to work immediately, but not later than Monday, July 7, 2025.

The Employer agrees to make health and welfare contributions in the months of July 2025 (June hours) for any employee whose store was on strike as of June 28, 2025, and August 2025 (July hours) for any employee whose store was on strike as of July 5, 2025, and who did not reach the necessary qualifying hours as set forth in Article 37 of the Agreement, so long as such individual qualified for July 2025 coverage based on May 2025 hours.

The Company agrees that within three (3) days of this Agreement it shall terminate, with the right to re-hire, employees who were hired in anticipation of or during the strike. No employee so re-hired shall be paid more than the entry rate of pay for the applicable job classification upon re-hire without working the requisite hours provided for under this Agreement or provides acceptable proof of relevant prior experience as provided for under this Agreement. Non-bargaining unit employees may perform bargaining unit work in excess of the limits set forth in the CBA, so long as: (1) any such work ceases within seven (7) days of the date of this Agreement, (2) such worker(s) did not work behind a picket line during the strike (except for non-bargaining unit management employees), and (3) the bargaining unit workers are first offered all hours being worked by such non-bargaining unit workers.

The Company shall reset all attendance points effective as of the date of ratification. The Union agrees to withdraw, on a non-precedent basis, but with prejudice, all Union All Affected grievances concerning unpaid Sunday Premium and the outsourcing of pharmacy work to Illinois (i.e., "Central Processing").

The parties will meet within 30 days of the execution of this Agreement to discuss a global settlement.

The Company will not consider the fact that an employee participated in the strike, picketed, or took any other action taken in connection with the strike for any future evaluation, promotion, merit, other raises, or discipline. Neither the Company nor the Union will retaliate or discriminate against any employee because of their participation in or refusal to participate in the strike, picketing or any other lawful action taken in connection with the strike. The Union reserves the right to discipline its members as provided for under its bylaws.

The parties agree to arbitrate all alleged violations of or disputes over the interpretation of this Agreement, or related to the subject matter of this Agreement in accordance with the parties' arbitration provisions in the newly agreed to CBA. Further, any grievances filed during the expiration of the CBAs in 2025 shall be subject to the arbitration provisions set forth in the parties' CBAs.

### **<u>TENTATIVE AGREEMENTS</u>**

**Revisions to Article 5 (All contracts except Rock Springs, Wyoming):**

### ARTICLE 5
### NEW EMPLOYEES, TRANSFERRED EMPLOYEES, PROMOTED OR DEMOTED

**(TA 3/13/25)** New Section. If the Union Security clause becomes unenforceable and void, the Employer agrees to provide a Union Representative (employee of the Union) fifteen (15) minutes for a new employee orientation with all new hires within their first 30 days of employment. Time spent in the New Employee Orientation will be considered time worked for the new employee.

**Revisions to Article 2 (Rock Springs, Wyoming):**

### ARTICLE 2
### UNION MEMBERSHIP

**(TA 3/13/25)** New Section. The Employer agrees to arrange an opportunity for newly hired employees (if they so choose) to meet with a Union Representative for up to 30 minutes for a New Employee Orientation within the employee's probationary period. The New Employee Orientation will not be considered hours worked.

**Revisions to Article 7:**

### ARTICLE 7
### DEFINITIONS OF CLASSIFICATIONS

**Section 14.**

For the purposes of this Agreement, the terms set forth below shall have the following meanings:

**(TA 5/23/25) h.** DRIVE UP AND GO. It is expressly understood and agreed that DUG Shopper work is and will remain bargaining unit work within the scope of the applicable "Clerks" collective bargaining agreements between Safeway Inc., Albertsons LLC., and UFCW Local 7 ~~within the Denver Division.~~ The Company agrees that it will not subcontract the shopping work involved in curbside customer pickup service (e.g. Drive Up and Go).

If the Company makes any changes to the DUG Program resulting in the elimination of the DUG department at a store, the Company shall inform the Union at least sixty (60) days prior to implementation of any such change or elimination.

DUG Shoppers will select and pack customer-ready products to fulfill customer orders. The DUG Shoppers will perform no preparation or cutting of food or meat.

DUG Shoppers shall be considered a separate classification in the Clerks Agreement for all purposes, including but not limited to seniority and scheduling.

Wage rates for DUG Shoppers will be the same as the Non-Food/GM classification wage rate progression of the applicable Clerks Agreement for the Store.

Where 3 or more DUG Shoppers are regularly assigned to that department, and where the Store does not already have such a position, the Company will post and select the most qualified individual to fill the role of DUG Supervisor (resulting in 1 supervisor and 2 clerks). The wage rate for the DUG Supervisor will be the same as the Head Clerk wage rate of the applicable Clerks agreement for the store.

<u>Section 15. Work Between Classifications:</u> ...

**(TA 11/6/24) Section 16. New Classifications.** When a new job is created by the Employer, the Union shall be notified immediately, and ~~a new wage rate for such job shall be determined by the Employer and the Union~~ shall meet within thirty (30) days to determine a wage rate for such job, unless otherwise extended by mutual agreement of the parties or as a result of an Act of God.

**Revisions to Article 8:**

# ARTICLE 8
# RATES OF PAY

*(Applies only to Meat Contracts)* Section 26. Tips. Coffee Bar Employees shall be permitted to accept tips. The Employer shall not assert any tip credit in order to reduce these employees' wages. Tips for coffee bar employees shall be pooled weekly and divided proportionally among coffee bar employees based on hours worked in the week.

*(Applies only to Estes Park)* Section 20. Summer Premium. Beginning in 2022, employees shall be entitled to a premium on all hours worked beginning the Sunday before Memorial Day and ending the Saturday following Labor Day. This premium shall be in the amount of one dollar and ten cents ($1.10) per hour for all hours worked. It shall not be subject to the overtime premium. Only employees whose home store is Estes Park (i.e., employees who do not receive mileage for travel to the Estes Park store) shall be eligible for the premium. The premium shall be paid on a weekly basis during the summer premium period described herein.

*(Applies only to Estes Park). Per Diem. Employees who travel from a different store to work in Estes Park shall be allowed a reimbursement per diem of up to $25 with receipts for each day where the employees travel and spend the night away from home.*

**(TA 12/18/24) Revisions to Article 9:**

# ARTICLE 9
# PRIOR EXPERIENCE

<u>Section 20.</u> In applying Section 19 of Article 8 of this Agreement to any newly hired employee, the Employer will give recognition to the verified number of hours of actual work experience on a comparable job which said newly hired employee may have performed within the previous ten (10) years for any other employer in a similar retail grocery operation, or other food operation including the Safeway Cake Commissary. The aforementioned shall include: Independent Floral, Liquor Stores, Independent Bakery, Starbucks, Delicatessen Shops, Pharmacy and King Soopers Fuel Stations. Service in the United States military or National Guard shall be given credit for one thousand forty (1040) hours per year of service, capped at four thousand, one hundred and sixty (4160) hours. This section shall only apply to newly hired employees upon ratification. <font color="red">The Company shall inform newly hired employees in writing at or before the time of onboarding that wage rate credits are available pursuant to this Agreement for employees who can document prior experience. An employee's wage rate will be adjusted as a result of this Section effective the first Sunday after the employee delivers documentation to the Company substantiating the prior experience.<sup>1</sup></font>

**Revisions to Article 10:**

# ARTICLE 10
# SCHEDULING AND ASSIGNMENT OF HOURS

**<u>Section 21. Work Schedules and Hours.</u>**

...

Not later than ten (10) days prior to the start of any workweek, management shall post a list of shifts for each department. Non-management, employees shall be allowed to select their schedule from the posted list of shifts for which they are qualified to perform, in seniority order, within their department. Full-time employees shall select first, followed by part-time employees. No employee shall be allowed to select a schedule that will result in overtime or other penalty provision, unless expressly authorized by management. The employee's selection shall be recorded on a master work schedule. Employees shall not be permitted to select a portion of a shift. Prior to the start of the selection process, management shall identify approved vacation requests on the schedule. <font color="red">(TA 1/4/25) Weekly shift selection shall take place for all departments unless the Employer and the Union mutually agree not to hold a shift selection in a given week for a given department.</font>

<font color="red"><u>Bargaining Note:</u> Union Stewards are not authorized to waive select a shift.</font>

Management may allow employees of one department to select shifts in another department. In this event, the employees must be qualified as defined herein, to perform the work of the other department.

**(TA 11/6/24)** Part-time Courtesy Clerks shall be scheduled for at least minimum hours unless otherwise agreed between the employee and management.

**(TA 1/4/25)** <u>Section 22. Department Bidding.</u> The Company shall allow during the first fifteen (15) days of February, to be effective the first workweek in March, and the first fifteen (15) days in August, to be effective the first workweek in September, non-management employees to bid ~~within their classification and the~~ store to another <u>retail bargaining unit</u> department. Management retains the right to determine the number of full-time and part-time positions in each department. If a senior employee from a department bids into another department, the least senior <u>non-courtesy clerk</u> employee in the <u>department</u>~~classification~~ and status affected shall be moved to the department vacated by the bidder. Employees may not ~~bid into a department if such bid will result in the displacement of a booth, dairy, service desk, order, produce or frozen food clerk,~~ unless the bidding employee has been previously classified as, trained for and worked, for six (6) months or longer within the last two (2) years, such position. <u>All non-management clerks, except courtesy clerks, shall be deemed eligible to bid into any non-pharmacy retail position, except as provided in the sentence above.</u> ~~Produce clerks may not bid out of the produce department unless an employee with the same status, who is qualified as described herein, has requested bid into the produce department.~~ The Employer agrees to provide training to <u>qualify</u> an employee <u>who is granted a</u> ~~to~~ bid into another department ~~as a grocery/GM stocker or as a checker.~~

**(TA 1/4/25)** *(Applies only to Meat contracts)* **Revisions to Article 27 (Meat):**

# <u>ARTICLE 27</u>
# <u>SENIORITY</u>

...

<u>New Section. Department Bidding. The Company shall allow during the first fifteen (15) days of February, to be effective the first workweek in March, and the first fifteen (15) days in August, to be effective the first workweek in September, non-management employees to bid within the store to another meat bargaining unit department. Management retains the right to determine the number of full-time and part-time positions in each department. If a senior employee from a department bids into another department, the least senior employee in the department and status affected shall be moved to the department vacated by the bidder. Employees may not displace a meatcutter. All non-management clerks shall be deemed eligible to bid into any meat position, except for meatcutter. The Employer agrees to provide training to an employee who is granted a bid into another department.</u>

**(TA 12/18/24) Revisions to Article 12:**

# ARTICLE 12
# OVERTIME

<u>Section 28.</u> Overtime compensation at the rate of time and one half (1 1/2X) the employee's ~~regular~~ base hourly rate of pay shall be paid under the following conditions:

a. For all time worked in excess of eight (8) hours in any one (1) day.

b. For all time worked in excess of forty (40) hours in any one (1) workweek as described above.

c. For hours worked prior to an employee's scheduled starting time when less than eight (8) hours has elapsed since his last previously scheduled quitting time. (There will be at least eight (8) hours between each employee's scheduled quitting time and his next scheduled starting time.)

d. For all hours scheduled and worked on the sixth and seventh day in a workweek by part-time employees who work less than forty (40) hours in that workweek. No employee shall be permitted to claim additional hours or schedules which would provide a six (6) or seven (7) day schedule during a workweek.

<u>For purposes of this Section, "regular hourly rate of pay" shall mean the hourly rate actually paid to employees for a standard, non-overtime workweek (including shift differentials, premiums, and incentive pays; excluding business expenses, bona fide gifts, discretionary bonuses<sup>2</sup>, pay for non-work hours, or other exclusions) as more fully defined pursuant to 7 Colo. Code Regs. 1103-1:1.8.<sup>3</sup></u>

**Revisions to Article 13:**

# ARTICLE 13
# SUNDAY PREMIUM

<u>Section 30.</u> The premium rate for work performed on Sunday as such shall be time and one quarter (1 1/4X) the employee's regular straight-time rate of pay (exclusive of Courtesy Clerks). The Sunday premium, for hours worked up to eight (8), shall in no instance be offset against any weekly overtime which may be due under subparagraphs b and d of Section 28 because of the fact that the employee worked over forty (40) hours or thirty-two (32) hours in the particular workweek. **(TA 12/18/24)** [~~The Sunday premium shall not be averaged into the employee's straight-time rate for the purpose of determining the rate upon which daily or weekly overtime is based in any workweek under Section 28 hereof.~~] Sunday premium pay for current Courtesy Clerks will be their regular rate of pay plus fifty cents ($.50) per hour.

Employees hired on or after March 27, 2005 shall not be eligible for Sunday Premium.

**Revisions to Article 14** *(Changes Proposed for Estes Park, Frisco, Gunnison, Leadville, Salida, Steamboat Springs, Vail)*

# ARTICLE 14
# TRAVEL PAY

<u>New Section. Mountain Travel Per Diem. Employees who perform temporary work at a mountain resort town store (defined as Vail, Steamboat Springs, Frisco, and Estes Park) and whose home store is a different store shall be entitled to standard mileage rate for travel.</u>

**Revisions to Article 15:**

# ARTICLE 15
# NIGHT PREMIUMS

Section 34. A premium of two dollars ($2.00) per hour shall be paid for all work performed between the hours of 12:00 p.m. midnight and 6:00 a.m. to all employees (excluding Courtesy Clerks).

All Courtesy Clerks shall receive <u>fifty</u>~~twenty-five~~ cents ($.50~~25~~) per hour in addition to the hourly rate for all work performed between the hours of 12:00 midnight and 6:00 a.m.

Night premium shall not apply where the employee is working at overtime or on Sunday or on a holiday.

**Revisions to Article 17 (additional proposals concerning Article 17 to be proposed at a later date):**

# ARTICLE 17
# VACATIONS

**(TA 4/22/25)** <u>Section 49</u><sup>4</sup>. Accrued and unused vacation shall roll over from anniversary year to anniversary year. Each employee who carries over two (2) or more weeks of vacation from one <u>anniversary</u> ~~calendar~~ year to the next, may make an irrevocable election <u>at least one month prior to their anniversary date</u> ~~in December~~ to take <u>up to two (2)</u> ~~one~~ weeks as vacation pay in lieu of time off in the subsequent <u>anniversary</u>~~calendar~~ year. <u>Such vacation pay in lieu of time off shall be paid out at the time of the employee's anniversary</u> ~~by January 31 of the calendar year~~ after the election is made. Employees' earned vacation banks are capped at two times their annual accrual. If the accrual cap is reached, accrual will stop until the earned vacation bank falls back below the cap, at which point accrual will begin again.

Bargaining note: It is understood that the provisions of this Section in no way modify the vacation scheduling language contained within this Agreement.

***

<sup>4</sup> <u>Changes to this section shall be effective beginning January 1, 2026, but payments for vacation pay in lieu of time off shall not be made until the employee's anniversary date.</u>

# <u>ARTICLE 27</u>

**(TA 3/13/25)** Look Back. Within ninety (90) days of ratification, the Employer will agree to review by store, in the trailing fifty-two (52) week period, ~~ending on the last Saturday of 2024~~ ~~December 31, 2021~~, to identify any part-time employee who during that period, worked, at straight-time plus vacation, a total of 2080 or more hours and post for seventy-two (72) hours, in the store where such employee worked the hours, the full-time opening(s) and to advance the most senior qualified employee who signs the posting to such position, or if no one signs the posting, to make the employee who worked the hours full time. The Employer agrees to an additional lookback at the beginning of year two (2) and year three (3) of the contract under the same terms. The Union agrees not to file any "4 at 40" grievances in the bargaining unit styled as Union All Affected during the life of the contract.

**(TA 5/23/25)** <u>Section 71. Promotions, Lateral Transfers, and Assignment to Full-Time.</u> The Employer agrees to make promotions and lateral transfers to non-management classifications and full-time status to the most senior qualified employee as provided herein. Management will post a list of openings on ~~the Career Opportunities on the Employer's web portal~~ ~~MyACI~~ and within the store where the opening exists for ~~ninety-six~~ ~~seventy-two~~ (~~96~~ ~~72~~) hours and said posting shall list the date and time the notice is posted. Employees may sign the posting and be considered for promotion. Upon completion of the ~~ninety-six~~ ~~seventy-two~~ (~~96~~ ~~72~~) hour period, management shall record the time it removed the posting and maintain a record of the posting for a period of no less than thirty (30) days. The Company shall offer the promotion/lateral transfer/full-time to the senior qualified employee within both the bargaining unit within the store, and, if none, then to the senior qualified employee within the store, and, if none, to the senior qualified employee not within the store, but within the bargaining unit, prior to hiring off-the-street.

**(TA 3/13/25) Section 74. Sister Company Credit.** When an employee transfers into the bargaining unit from any Albertson's store in Colorado or Wyoming, the Company shall honor the employee's most recent hire date with Albertson's and/or Safeway for all purposes except scheduling, layoffs, vacation bidding, department bidding, full-time status, promotions, and overtime. Specifically, eligibility for health care benefits shall be from the employee's most recent hire date with Albertson's and/or Safeway.

> **BARGAINING NOTE:** For purposes of this provision, the phrase "most recent hire date with Albertson's and/or Safeway" means the most recent date of continuous employment with either banner.

**(TA 12/2/24) Revisions to Article 29.**

## ARTICLE 29
## LAYOFF

Section 84. Demotions ~~and Step Downs~~.

---

<sup>* In Albertsons CBAs, this will say Safeway. In Safeway CBAs, this will say Albertsons.</sup>

1. If a member of the bargaining unit classified as a Head Clerks or above is demoted, or steps down, ~~voluntarily or involuntarily,~~ and has been employed in the bargaining unit for a minimum of one continuous year prior to the demotion, the employee ~~shall~~ may be returned to the classification and status, full-time or part-time, when first promoted to the bargaining unit position of Head Clerk or above. In returning the employee to the position previously held, the least senior employee in the classification and status may be bumped as a result. Further, the Company may demote the employee to a bargaining unit management position as long as the assignment does not circumvent the Collective Bargaining Agreement.

2. If a member of the bargaining unit classified as a Head Clerk or above is demoted or steps down, ~~voluntarily or involuntarily,~~ and has been employed in the bargaining unit for a minimum of one continuous year prior to the demotion, but has not held a non-management position in the bargaining unit, he ~~shall~~ may claim ~~a position as if he had signed the full-time or promotion request lists~~ an open position posted on the Employer's web portal and may bump the junior incumbent employee based on seniority.

3. If a member of the bargaining unit classified as Head Clerk of above is demoted or steps down, ~~voluntarily or involuntarily,~~ and has not been employed in the bargaining unit for one continuous year prior to the demotion, the employee shall be placed in the position of a Courtesy Clerk.

4. If a management employee who is not a member of the bargaining unit is demoted, or steps down ~~voluntarily or involuntarily,~~ into a non-management bargaining unit position, the employee ~~shall~~ may exercise full Company seniority from the date of such demotion, notwithstanding language set forth in the Collective Bargaining Agreement establishing a 30 day waiting period, ~~and will be deemed to have signed the full-time and promotion request lists and to have all rights available to an employee on such lists.~~ Such an employee, however, may not bump an incumbent employee from a position but must await a vacancy which he ~~shall~~ may claim based on his seniority as provided for in the full-time and promotion request procedures. Pending a vacancy, the employee ~~shall,~~ may at Company discretion, be placed either as a management trainee as defined in the Collective Bargaining Agreement or a Courtesy Clerk. Further, the employee must be employed for one continuous year in a store or facility covered by any Collective Bargaining Agreement with Local 7 immediately preceding the demotion or the employee shall be placed in the position of Courtesy Clerk.

5. The Company may demote a management employee who is not a member of the bargaining unit into a management bargaining unit position of Head Clerk or above so long as such assignment does not circumvent the Collective Bargaining Agreement.

6. When a reduction in the number of employees in a classification of Head Clerk and above is implemented, this procedure shall not apply, but rather this Article ~~the Letter of Understanding~~ concerning layoff of bargaining unit management personnel shall be followed.

7. ~~This Settlement Agreement shall apply to all Collective Bargaining Agreements between Safeway and Local 7 in Colorado and shall have a term coextensive with the current collective bargaining agreements.~~

8. ~~Local 7 agrees that the arbitrator in the Monte Vista Reduction of Hours arbitration, Union case #644-85, currently pending ("Monte Vista Arbitration") will not be advised of either the fact or terms of this Letter of Understanding and that this Letter of Understanding shall not be used as evidence in any way in the Monte Vista Arbitration.~~

**(TA 3/13/25) Revision to Article 28<sup>6</sup>:**

# ARTICLE 28
# UNSCHEDULED OVERTIME

Section 76. Unscheduled Overtime Hours. Daily overtime not previously scheduled shall be offered in seniority order within the department, the classification and the store, to the employees present when the need for overtime arises. Nothing herein shall be construed to require the scheduling of overtime when another employee's scheduled hours can be extended or part-time employees may be called in without overtime penalty. Hours unclaimed under this procedure may be assigned in reverse order of seniority among those employees within the department within the classification within the store present when the need for overtime arises.

Overtime assignments of four (4) hours or more may be filled by calling in employees, in seniority order, within the classification and the department on their non-scheduled day without violating this Section. <span style="color:red">Employees who have marked themselves as unavailable for the day do not need to be called.</span>

<span style="color:red">Bargaining Note: It is understood that to be considered unavailable, the employee would need to communicate their unavailability in writing in a reasonable format provided by the Company.</span>

**Revision to Article 33**

# ARTICLE 33
# BEREAVEMENT LEAVE



![Handwritten Initials]

**(TA 4/18/25) Section 95.** Upon request, an employee covered by this Agreement shall be granted the necessary time off with pay at his regular straight-time rate of pay in order to make arrangements for and/or attend a funeral occasioned by a death in his immediate family. Such time off with pay shall in no event exceed three (3) regularly scheduled working days. The immediate family is defined as the employee's father, mother, step-parents, grandparents, grandchildren, spouse, common-law spouse, an individual in a civil union with that employee if recognized by State law, children, step-child, brother, sister; and father, mother, brother and sister of the then existing spouse. Payments shall not be made hereunder where the relative's death occurs while the employee is on vacation or on a leave of absence.

Additional time, without pay, shall be granted as is needed by the employee up to seven (7) days for the above defined immediate family as well as for aunts, uncles, nieces, nephews, first cousins, step-brother, step-sisters, co-parents, fiancés/fiancées and grandparent of the then existing spouse.

<u>Bargaining Note:</u> For unique circumstances, the Company and the Union will meet to discuss any additional needs for leave under this section.

**Revisions to Article 36:**

# <u>ARTICLE 36</u>
# <u>SAFETY</u>

**(TA 6/11/25)** <u>New Section. The Employer shall not discipline or penalize in any way an employee who is tardy or fails to appear for the employee's scheduled shift in the event the absence or tardy is due to the unforeseen or unavoidable consequences of inclement weather. An employee experiencing such a circumstance must still take reasonable efforts to notify the Employer as soon as practicable.</u>

<u>Section 108. Master Safety Committee.</u> The Employer and the Union will jointly set up a Master Safety Committee, made up of two (2) members from the Union and two (2) members from the Company, to discuss and work toward resolving safety issues in the workplace.

The Master Safety committee will meet periodically, and no less frequently than once per quarter, to review workplace safety matters. The parties will discuss and work toward resolving safety in the workplace.

In addition, the Company and the Union agree that they will continue to discuss and jointly address safety related issues and/or questions about the Company's safety program in good faith.

**(TA 4/10/25)** <u>The Union and the Employer agree that the prevention of violence in the store and the safekeeping of employees in the workplace is of utmost importance. As such, the parties agree that these issues are appropriate topics of discussion in Master Safety Committee meetings. Discussion may include potential government lobbying efforts.</u>

<u>Dangerous Emergencies.</u> The Employer will develop procedures that workers should follow to protect themselves and co-workers during dangerous emergencies. These procedures may include: (i) where workers should go to protect themselves, (ii) evacuation plans, (iii) what

workers should do, and (iv) how prompt first aid and emergency medical treatment will be administered to injured workers. The procedures will also discuss signs that may indicate that a dangerous emergency may occur (such as threats, social media posts or assaults), and encourage workers, customers and others to report these matters to a manager or security guard, if applicable. The Employer will update the training as new procedures to protect workers against dangerous emergencies develop. (TA 4/10/25) ~~If the Employer becomes aware of such an emergency, management will notify employees of the existence of an emergency that reasonably exposes the employees to serious danger, unless the nature of the emergency makes notification unsafe. The Employer will follow any instructions it may receive from law enforcement or other government authority.~~

The "up to" rates for ~~2023 and 2024~~ **2026 and 2027** will be determined as following:

1. Using the latest financial data available as of **each September (or most recently available data in preparation for the December fund meeting)**, co-consultants will develop a forecast through 12/31/202~~4~~**7**.
2. In preparing the forecast, the below trend rates will be used.
3. If the forecast projects an ending balance at 12/31/202~~4~~**7** that is below the target reserve level (average of ~~2.9~~**1.4** months of expense for the 12 months ending 12/31/202~~4~~**7**, ~~plus IBNR at 12/31/2024~~), then the employer contributions will be increased effective January ~~2023 and 2024~~ **2026 and 2027** so that the ending reserve will be equal to the target reserve. Any projected deficit in the ending balance shall first be corrected by increasing the 202~~3~~**6** employer contribution rates until such rates reach the "up to" levels for 202~~3~~**6**.
4. In no event will the increase in the employer contributions rates exceed 5.0% in 2026 or 2027~~3 or 2024~~. In no event will the "up to" employer contribution rates be less than the prior year's employer contribution rate.
5. Co-consultants will work together to develop increases that are as close as possible. In the event co-consultants develop materially different estimates, the lowest increase will be implemented while Trustees resolve the differences between the two estimates of the co-consultants. Any arbitration concerning the differences between the two estimates shall be held not more than sixty (60) days following deadlock.

**<u>Initial Eligibility</u>** –

...

On-going Eligibility – After satisfying initial eligibility requirement provisions and enrollment in the Health Plan, the employee must continue to meet the monthly on-going eligibility requirements as a condition of continued participation in the Health Plan. Enrolled employees who work (80) hours in a (4) week month or (100) hours in a (5) week month shall be eligible for coverage on a lag month basis. For the purpose of this Article, hours worked shall include hours paid directly by the Company for **(TA 12/19/24) overtime,<sup>8</sup>** holiday, vacation, jury duty, funeral leave, and sick leave.

Employees shall continue to be eligible for benefits provided they enroll for coverage in accordance with this Article. In any event, all employees must continue to meet all eligibility requirements of the Plan as a condition of continued eligibility.

<u>Trust Plan Changes.</u>

...

Effective January 1, ~~2026~~ <u>2020, Plan B's</u> the dental benefit <u>for all plans</u> shall become identical to the dental benefit for Plan A. Effective January 1, 2020, any employee and their dependents who are enrolled in Plan B shall receive the improved dental benefit. <u>Effective January 1, 2026, the maximum annual dental benefit shall be increased to $2,000.</u>

<u>Effective January 1, 2026, the following plan changes shall be made:</u>

* <u>The (biennial) lens benefit (glasses and contact lenses) shall be doubled<sup>9</sup>, and a $10 co-pay shall be added for basic vision exams, which shall be a separate benefit from the lens allowance.</u>
* <u>The death benefit shall be increased to $15,000.</u>

<u>Further, the bargaining parties recommend to the Trustees that going forward the fund conduct a dependent audit at least once every three (3) years, starting in 2027. In addition, the bargaining parties recommend to the Trustees that at least once during the term of the 2025-2028 agreement, the Trustees conduct a RFP process for pharmacy benefit managers to include consideration of the scope of the network and appropriate formulary.</u>

# ARTICLE 50
# DISPUTE PROCEDURE

Section 149. Step 2. In an instance where an employee feels he has not been paid in accordance with the wage progression scales set forth herein, such employee shall have an obligation to bring this to the attention of the Store Manager as soon as the employee first has knowledge of such alleged error. In the event the employee has been improperly paid, said payment error shall be corrected on a retroactive basis, but not beyond ninety (90) days prior to the date on which the grievance is presented in writing. <u>This ninety (90) day retroactive liability shall not be applicable to situations covered by Article 8, Section 25a, second paragraph. In such situations, in accordance with Article 8, Section 25a, the retroactive liability will be adjusted to the first Sunday after the employee delivers documentation to the Company substantiating the prior experience.</u>

**Revisions to Article 52:**

# ARTICLE 52
# UNIFORMS/EQUIPMENT

**(TA 1/4/25)** Section 158. The Employer agrees to provide all required uniforms and laundry service for all required caps, uniforms, smocks, aprons, towels and rags, except for laundering of drip-dry garments. The employee agrees to exercise care in the use of Company property and equipment.

Notwithstanding the above, the employee shall be required to meet the dress requirements as detailed in <u>this Article.</u> ~~the Letter of Understanding, "Dress Requirements," attached to this Agreement.~~

<u>New Section. The Employer provided name badge must be worn while on duty. Employees must wear pants of wool, cotton, knit, or non-faded denim material in good condition and repair, which shall be provided by the employee. Sweats, stirrup pants, stretch pants, painter pants, spandex, etc. are prohibited. Employees will be allowed to wear clothing worn in accordance with religious obligation. Shoes must be clean and in good condition. Open toe or open heel shoes are not permitted. Courtesy Clerks and DUG Associates may wear shorts between May 1 and September 30 provided they are of the same material allowed above.</u>

<u>The Employer and the Union will meet and confer in good faith ninety (90) days prior to the implementation of any change to the dress code. Any such change shall not impose any undue economic burden on the bargaining unit employees. Any dress code which requires Company logo apparel shall be paid for by the Employer.</u>

**(TA 11/21/24) Revisions to Article 56:**

# ARTICLE 56
# PHARMACY TECHNICIANS

<u>New Section<sup>11</sup>. Technician Vaccine Administration. Pharmacy Technicians are allowed to administer vaccines under the following terms:</u>

1. <u>Non-Certified Pharmacy Technicians and current Certified Technicians will be offered the opportunity to administer vaccines. If they decline, they will not be forced to administer vaccines nor will they suffer any adverse consequences as a direct result of making this choice.</u>
2. <u>New Hire Certified Technicians: New Certified Pharmacy Technicians will be required to administer vaccines, pursuant to the terms of this Agreement.</u>
3. <u>Vaccination Premium. During the term of this Agreement, all Pharmacy Technicians who give vaccinations, current and new hires, will receive a $2.25 per hour premium for all hours worked once they have been trained to give immunizations and immunizations are available at their store.</u>
4. <u>Training. All required and necessary training to give immunizations will be paid for and provided by the Company.</u>
5. <u>Bonuses: In order to aid the Company to attract the talent required, the Company can offer the following bonuses, where appropriate (i.e., at store(s) selected by the Company in its discretion) to new employees.</u>
    a. <u>Signing Bonus: the Company can offer an $800 signing bonus to newly hired Technicians that will be paid out $300 at hire, $300 after 6 months, and $200 after 9 months.</u>
    b. <u>Referral Bonus. The Company can offer a referral bonus to current associates who successfully refer candidates for pharmacy technician job openings that will be paid out $250 at hire and $250 after the hired technician has been in position for 6 months.</u>
6. <u>Safety & Liability: The Company will continue to provide appropriate PPE for Technicians who give immunizations. The Denver Division will provide blood borne pathogens training (as it does now), CPR training, and will provide secure disposal tools for SHARPS that have been used to immunize patients. Pharmacy Technicians will be covered under the Company's liability insurance.</u>

<u>New Section<sup>12</sup>. Float Pool. The Employer may establish a certified pharmacy technician Float Pool within each District.</u>

<u>A "Floater" is a Certified Pharmacy Technician who the Employer regularly assigns to work in more than one store.</u>

The Employer shall not have any obligation to use Floaters at any time. If the Employer elects to use Floaters it shall be done in accordance with the following general principles:

Each Float Pool shall be on a district wide basis. Each district's Float Pool shall be deemed a separate store for all purposes under this Agreement, including full-time status language.

No Certified Pharmacy Technician may be assigned to the Float Pool without their consent. Prior to hiring a Floater pharmacy technician from outside the bargaining unit, the Employer must comply with Promotions, Lateral Transfers, and Assignment to Full-Time process described herein.

Management shall schedule Floaters on the basis of seniority up to eight (8) hours per day and forty (40) hours per week to stores where there are available pharmacy technician hours within the district. It is understood that all Certified Pharmacy Technicians within the store will be offered the hours (if available) prior to assigning a Floater to the store. The seniority of Floaters shall be honored based on the hours made available by the stores, so that Floaters are scheduled to the fewest number of stores as practicable each week. Management shall offer vacated shifts (whether by operation of this Agreement or as a result of a call off) within the store first pursuant to the Available Hours provision, and if not claimed then to the Floaters in the Float Pool in the district who have not maximized hours in seniority order.

Floaters shall have the right to claim full or part-time Certified Pharmacy Technician vacancies which become available in the stores before the Employer may hire from outside the bargaining unit. The Employer shall not utilize the Float Pool as a means to avoid filling long-term needs. It is understood that the Floater Pharmacy Technicians shall be subject to the same minimum hours provisions (set forth elsewhere in this Agreement) as store-based Pharmacy Technicians.

Reduction of full-time Floaters shall be pursuant to the Reduction of Hours provision set forth elsewhere in this agreement. Full-time Floaters desiring full-time non-floating assignments may request the same in writing to the person designated by the Employer, and such assignment shall be made in seniority order when such opening occurs.

The store nearest the home of each Floater shall be designated as that Floater's home store within the District. Employees shall be entitled to mileage to stores other than their home store.

This Certified Pharmacy Technician Floater program shall remain in effect for the duration of this Collective Bargaining Agreement.

**Revisions to Article 57:**

# ARTICLE 57
# TERM OF AGREEMENT

**Section 174.** This Agreement shall be in full force and effect beginning at 12:01 a.m. on ~~January 9, 2022~~ January 5, 2025 and shall remain in full force and effect until ~~11:59 p.m. midnight on January 4, 2025~~ January 8, 2028<sup>13</sup> and shall be automatically renewed from year to year thereafter, unless either party desires change or termination at the expiration of said Agreement. In such event, the party desiring such change or termination shall notify the other party in writing sixty (60) days prior to the expiration date, specifying the changes desired. Changes in the Agreement shall be limited to those outlined in writing by either party and the negotiations shall begin within fifteen (15) days after receipt of such notice.

**Proposed Revision to Appendix A:**

# APPENDIX "A"

The Employer agrees that for those positions identified with a grandfathered rate on the attached wage tables, any individual who held a classification and rate so identified as of January 11, 2022, shall be grandfathered during the term of this Agreement at fifty cents ($0.50) over the otherwise applicable wage rate, and shall receive the benefit of future increases. This rate is reflected on the attached wage charts as "grandfathered."

<u>Additionally, any employee being paid above the wage scale as of the date of ratification shall maintain the increased pay and receive the benefit of all future wage increases. For example, a Denver City Head Clerk is paid $25.11 (even though the contract rate is $24.11). Upon ratification, the Head Clerk would be paid one dollar more than the rate for a Head Clerk. With each pay raise, the Head Clerk would continue to make one dollar more than the wage scale rate.</u>

<u>(applies only in Albertsons Meat Contracts) All Seafood Managers employed at the time of ratification shall be grandfathered, and shall receive the benefit of all future pay increases.</u>

**<u>SEE ATTACHED WAGE TABLES</u>**

**(TA 6/11/25)** Basket Hours. ...

Similarly, an employee that moves from a higher classification to a lower classification, except an employee moving to meat cutter, will receive credit for all hours <u>(or months, in the case of an employee moving to Courtesy Clerk)</u> worked with the company and those hours <u>(or months, in the case of an employee moving to Courtesy Clerk)</u> will determine their pay level in the new classification (even if this results in a decrease in pay).

**Replace Letter of Understanding regarding Minimum Wage with the following Letter of Understanding:**

### LETTER OF UNDERSTANDING
### MINIMUM WAGE

Effective on ratification, the starting rate in any job classification, excluding courtesy clerks, in stores subject to the Colorado statewide minimum wage, shall be not less than forty cents ($0.40) above the operative minimum wage applicable to the store, and each rate above will be at least twenty-five cents ($0.25) per hour higher than the previous rate in the progression schedule.

<u>Effective on ratification, the starting rate in any job classification in stores subject to a local minimum wage (not equal to the statewide minimum wage), shall be not less than the operative minimum wage applicable to the store, and each rate above will be at least twenty-five cents ($0.25) per hour higher than the previous rate in the progression schedule. The parties agree that the Thereafter rates for stores subject to a local minimum wage (not equal to the statewide minimum wage) will not be increased by the operation of this Letter of Understanding (and that no progression rate will exceed the Thereafter rate).</u>

Bargaining Note: In applying the provisions of this Letter, the parties understand, for example, that an employee working at a progression step that is adjusted as a result of the operation of this letter would remain at the same step but work under the newly adjusted rate until they complete the remaining hours of that step and advance to the next step.

### LETTER OF UNDERSTANDING
### Vail, Frisco and Steamboat Springs, Colorado
### Addendum Agreement

1. Beginning in 1990, the Employer shall pay a bonus of ten percent (10%) of gross earnings to all employees employed as of Saturday following Easter Sunday.
2. The bonus shall be paid on all hours paid up to forty (40) per week for the (ski season)period from the first full week prior to Thanksgiving through the Saturday following Easter Sunday.

**(TA 1/23/25) Revisions to Letter of Understanding 2:**

2. C-14 Procedure for Scheduling Employees with Conscientious Objections to Working on Their Day of Sabbath. Unsigned and undated agreement between Safeway and UFCW Local 7.

### PROCEDURE FOR SCHEDULING EMPLOYEES WITH CONSCIENTIOUS OBJECTIONS TO WORKING ON THEIR DAY OF SABBATH

~~We have had a number of requests for the procedure in the handling of employees scheduled on a day which is their day of Sabbath.~~ Safeway has entered into an agreement with UFCW which provides certain procedures for accommodating individuals who have such conscientious objections.

Problems can result in a grievance under the contract as well as a possible violation of the laws against discrimination on the basis of religion, ~~so please follow these procedures carefully and call Safeway Inc. Human Resources if necessary.~~ ~~Per Article 43, Section 126,~~ the Employer and the Union will fully comply with the applicable laws and regulations

~~prohibiting discrimination against any employee, or applicant for employment, because of such person's religion. Employees may request a reasonable accommodation for schedules due to a conscientious religious objection to working a particular day of the week.~~

This procedure, of course, applies only to any employee who advised ~~you~~ their management:

1. that they have conscientious objections to working a particular day of the week.
2. the nature of their conscientious objections, and
3. the particular day of the week which they are unable to work.

~~If you have any questions concerning whether the employee actually has bona fide conscientious objections, be certain to contact Employee Relations and review the matter. You also should~~ Managers will complete the form attached to these instructions, ask the employee to sign it, and route it to Safeway Inc. Human Resources Department for ~~future reference.~~ review and approval.

The procedure for scheduling is as follows:

1. Until noon on Saturday for the following week's schedule an employee may identify and request an exchange of shifts with any employee junior to him in the same job classification in the store which will result in the employee obtaining their Sabbath as a day off. ~~You may deny this~~ This request may be denied, if the exchange would require an employee to perform duties for which they are not trained, or for some other equally substantial business reason. Otherwise ~~you must grant the~~ the request must be granted. Seniority shall prevail, and the junior employee cannot refuse to make the trade.

2. As an option, an employee may identify and request an exchange of shifts with a senior employee who is willing to make such an exchange. Again, ~~you may deny this~~ request may be denied if the exchange would require an employee to perform duties for which they are not trained, or for some other equally substantial business reason. Otherwise ~~you must grant the~~ request must be granted. Seniority shall prevail and the senior employee may refuse to make the trade.

3. As a third alternative, an employee may simply decline to work on their day of Sabbath if they cannot trade shifts with anyone else. Such an employee will not be disciplined under the Absenteeism Program except for failure to notify the Company prior to a scheduled shift that he will not work on their day of Sabbath. ~~You will then~~ The employee would be assessed points for failure to call, but not for the absence itself.

4. If an employee cannot make a change of shifts and is scheduled on their day of Sabbath for the entire bid period or for any extended period of time, it is permissible for that employee to advise ~~you~~ management at the beginning of the bid period or

> other extended period of time that they will not work on such day for the entire three months. Such an employee, if full-time, will not in fact be scheduled 40 hours, but 32 hours. The Company has no obligation to provide 40 hours work under these circumstances.

Attached ~~you will find~~ is a form for keeping a record of any such scheduling accommodation to be completed by Management.

~~It is very important that we follow these procedures and complete the attached form in the event we are challenged on our application of the settlement agreement.~~

# Store Manager Company Response:

(Was Request Granted, and if not, State Specifically why not)

For: Safeway/Albertsons  
For: UFCW Local 7  

Date  
Date  

(TA 5/23/25) Replace the following Letter of Understanding (B-1):

1. The Company will agree to replace the existing letter of understanding (B-1) concerning the alcohol and drug rehabilitation program with the following:

The Employer and Union mutually agree to the following Alcohol and Substance Abuse Policy:

A. If the Employer has reasonable cause to believe that an employee in the bargaining unit is impaired by a controlled substance or alcohol during working hours or on Company premises, or in the event of an accident or injury to either the employee or another person requiring medical attention beyond basic first aid, the Employer shall have the right to require the employee to submit to a urinalysis or other generally accepted test. The Employer shall pay for the expense of the test. Any employee who refuses such test shall be immediately discharged. The Employer also has the right to choose not to require a drug or alcohol test. Any discipline the Employer issues pursuant to the terms of this paragraph is naturally subject to the just cause standard based on the evidence.

B. If the test is positive for a controlled substance or alcohol and it is the employee’s first offense of such nature which is not in conjunction with any other related gross misconduct, the employee will be given the opportunity to enter an Employer approved rehabilitation program, unless the employee had previously attended, or been given the opportunity to attend, a rehabilitation program through Safeway. If the employee accepts rehabilitation, the employee shall be given a disciplinary suspension and final warning for the period of rehabilitation. Nothing in this Agreement shall be construed to conflict with a Colorado employee’s FAMLI rights. An employee who fails to complete the rehabilitation program under this paragraph shall be immediately discharged. Any discipline the Employer issues pursuant to the terms of this paragraph is naturally subject to the just cause standard based on the evidence.

C. If the employee refuses rehabilitation, the employee shall be immediately discharged. The employee shall release and/or supply to the Employer and the Union a written

report of the results of the test. The Employer shall not use its rights to test to harass an employee. Further, if an employee voluntarily approaches Management prior to being required to submit to testing and indicates that the employee has a drug, substance abuse, or alcohol problem, and no other gross misconduct is involved, the Employer will give the employee a leave of absence (some or all of which may be with FAMLI leave benefits) to enroll in a drug or alcohol rehabilitation program. The employee will continue to a leave of absence for the period of rehabilitation, but not to exceed the maximum leave provisions of the Agreement or as required by law, without any loss of seniority. Nothing in the Agreement shall be construed to require the Employer to grant an employee more than one leave of absence, or provide more than one opportunity for rehabilitation.

D. An employee shall not be eligible for rehabilitation as provided for under this policy in the event that an employee's violation of this policy occurs in combination with any other act of gross misconduct (for example: drinking on the job, use of a controlled substance on the job, sale of a controlled substance on Company premises, dishonesty, violence or attempted violence against a coworker or supervisor, etc.).

E. Employee Request for Treatment. As a result of voluntary self-referral, an employee shall have the opportunity to seek treatment for, and to correct substance abuse or dependency. The employee will be granted a medical leave of absence for the purpose of enrolling and participating in a recognized and approved rehabilitation program. The program shall be at the employee's expense to the extent not covered by health insurance as provided in the collective bargaining agreement. Upon release to report back to work, the employee may be required to submit to unscheduled follow-up testing for a period not to exceed 24 months. Refusal to comply with such testing or any follow-up test results indicating the presence of a controlled substance or alcohol will result in immediate discharge. The provisions of this Section shall not apply to probationary employees.

***

**Add New Letter of Understanding:**

# LETTER OF UNDERSTANDING
# STAFFING

### 1. General Staffing

As provided in the parties' CBAs, Management retains the right to determine weekly work schedules to accommodate the needs of the business, including the right to determine the number of hours, and start times of each shift, to be worked within each department and store. Notwithstanding the foregoing, the Employer agrees that staffing decisions will be made in good faith and consistent with the considerations set forth herein. The Employer agrees to maintain reasonable staffing levels at all times to ensure the efficient operation of the store, the health and safety of employees, and the quality of customer service. Staffing decisions shall take into account the store's operational needs, customer volume, and other factors affecting store performance, including but not limited to peak hours, seasonal fluctuations, and special promotions.

### 2. Consultation and Communication

The Employer shall, within reason, provide the Union with the opportunity to review staffing reports upon request. If any information requested is considered confidential, the parties agree to sign an NDA prior to such information being provided. In addition, the Employer agrees to discuss with the Union if there are significant concerns regarding staffing levels at a store or stores. Staffing shall be either a standing agenda item on the Joint Labor Management Committee agenda or on the agenda of a separate Staffing Committee.

The Parties shall establish a Staffing Committee. The Staffing Committee shall be comprised as follows:

1. Within 45 days, following ratification, the employer and a committee will meet to discuss staffing levels within the stores and shall meet thereafter as the parties may mutually agree, up to once a quarter.

2. Employer may designate up to four (4) members of management as part of the committee. The Union may designate up to four (4) officials of the Union or Department Heads or Head Clerks as part of the committee.

3. Upon mutual agreement, the Company and the Union may invite other individuals to attend a meeting of the committee.

4. The staffing committee shall meet at least three (3) times per year either independently or through the Joint Labor Management Committee. This minimum may be satisfied if the Staffing Committee meets through the Joint Labor Management Committee, unless otherwise mutually agreed.

The Committee shall meet at least twice within six (6) months following ratification to discuss potential staffing ideas to test. If the Committee reaches a joint recommendation, the Company

will agree to test the staffing adjustments in up to 8 locations<sup>14</sup> as a test and learn. The Committee may review the results of any pilot following the start of such test program. The data necessary to monitor and audit any pilot shall be sent to the agreed upon union designees. Union designees shall operate under a non-disclosure agreement when analyzing this data and will only share said data when it is necessary for a grievance or other enforcement action and only to the extent required for enforcement. It is agreed that the Employer may discontinue a given test and learn at its discretion. Conversely, the Employer may expand a test program beyond the original test stores at its discretion.

3. This Letter of Understanding shall continue in effect from ratification of the 2025-2028 Collective Bargaining Agreement until either party provides written notice of cancellation to the other or of its desire to modify or not pull this Letter forward as a part of a new agreement. The cancelling party shall provide 30 days' notice of cancellation and such cancellation shall not be effective until expiration of the 2025-2028 agreement (or anytime thereafter).

***

**Revisions to Article 49:**

### ARTICLE 49
### UNION STEWARD

**(TA 11/21/24)** Section 143. The Union shall have the right to designate one (1) Steward per store (stores that have 20 or more employees in the meat bargaining unit may have two (2) Stewards) who shall perform their Steward duties in such a way as not to interfere with the service of the Employer. In stores with more than one Steward, it is agreed that one Steward may come from a given subdepartment (meat, deli). Such Stewards shall have top seniority for the purpose of layoff within their classification in that store. The designated representative of the Employer must be advised in writing by the Union of the name of the Steward in the store before the employee will be recognized as a Steward.

Stewards shall not be bumped from their respective stores by employees exercising their second (2<sup>nd</sup>) or their eleventh (11<sup>th</sup>) week bump, unless the Steward chooses to do so.
